--- COURSE STRUCTURE ---

HCDE 530 — competency-based assessment across 8 domains (C1–C8).
Grade is built from competency claims backed by evidence in the GitHub repo, not points on assignments.

The Eight Competency Domains:
- C1 — Vibecoding and Rapid Prototyping
- C2 — Code Literacy and Documentation
- C3 — Data Cleaning and File Handling
- C4 — APIs and Data Acquisition
- C5 — Data Analysis with Pandas
- C6 — Data Visualization
- C7 — Critical Evaluation and Professional Judgment
- C8 — Building and Deploying a Complete Tool

--- WEEKLY ASSIGNMENTS COMPLETED ---

Week 2 — C2 (Code Literacy & Documentation)
- demo_word_count.py + demo_dashboard.html on demo_responses.csv
- count_words() with docstrings; Path(__file__) for portable paths
- response_word_analysis.py exports word stats CSV
- Competency claim in Week 2/week2.md

Week 3 — C2 + C3 (Data Cleaning)
- clean_responses.py pipeline: drop empty names, normalize roles → responses_cleaned.csv
- count_roles.py → role_counts.csv
- week3_analysis_buggy.py: 8-theme keyword analysis of survey text; fixed ValueError
  from non-numeric data and sorting logic bug
- Competency claims in Week 3/week3.md (notes early vague commit messages as C2 gap)

Week 4 — A4 (APIs) [C4]
- Called Pexels Search API for pharmacy stock images
- Three-script pipeline in Week 4/:
  - export_pexels_to_csv.py — fetched 50+ photos, extracted 12 fields from nested JSON
  - download_pexels_csv_images.py — downloaded JPEGs from CDN URLs
  - analyze_pexels_shape_color.py — classified pill shape and color via alt-text regex + Pillow pixel analysis fallback
- Second API: hcde530-week4-api.onrender.com/reviews for app reviews with VADER sentiment analysis
- API keys stored in .env via os.environ.get
- Competency claim written for C4

Week 5 — A5 (Pandas) [C5]
- Analyzed HYG v4.2 star catalog (119,626 real stars) in Week 5/MP1/a5_analysis.ipynb
- Used all five pandas operations: head, info, describe, isnull().sum(), filtering, value_counts, groupby
- Three analysis questions:
  1. Can stars cluster into constellation-like groups? (K-Means with k=88 on RA/Dec)
  2. Do bright stars anchor clusters? (box plot — ~3 bright anchors per cluster)
  3. Do clusters have different stellar populations? (spectral class composition)
- Built custom cat constellation "Felis" using anatomy-dictionary approach
- Key finding: all nine matched stars landed at mag 5.3–6.3, not near famous bright stars

Week 6 — A6 / MP1b (Visualization) [C5, C6]
- Built MP1/mp1b_visualizations.ipynb with four Plotly charts:
  - Chart 1: Felis 2D sky scatter (Relationship — Abela framework)
  - Chart 1b: Felis 3D Cartesian (honest companion showing projection artifact)
  - Chart 2: Brightness box plot per cluster (Distribution)
  - Chart 3: Spectral composition 100% stacked bar (Composition)
- Also: Week 6/plotly-exercises.ipynb, tidy_data_exercise.ipynb (FlowNote tidy data),
  bird_strikes.csv, clean_ufo_data.csv class datasets
- Key insight: 3D cat was unrecognizable because anchor stars sit 49–411 parsecs apart —
  constellation shape is a projection artifact, not a physical structure

Week 7 — Figma user feedback dataset
- Week 7/week7_figma_feedback.csv — 22 curated public comments on Figma UI3 migration
  and editor UX failures (forced migration, workflow slowdown, accessibility complaints)

Week 8 — MP2a declaration + prepare_stars.py data pipeline for Twinkle

--- MAJOR PROJECT: MP1 — STAR CATALOG ANALYSIS ---

File: MP1/mp1b_visualizations.ipynb
Dataset: HYG v4.2 (astronexus.com/hyg) — 119,626 stars, filtered to 8,834 naked-eye visible (mag < 6.5)
Five sections: Overview, Data Profile, Analysis (4 charts), Conclusions, Process narrative

Key findings:
- Custom constellations can be built from real stars but snap to dim stars not bright anchors —
  generator should prioritize brightness over proximity
- Every cluster has same right-skewed brightness distribution: 2–4 bright anchors + many dim fillers
- Hot star share varies 14.7%–44.1% across clusters — sky regions are astrophysically distinct

Competency claims: C5, C6, C7, C2

--- MAJOR PROJECT: MP2 — TWINKLE (twinkle.ltd) ---

Live site: https://twinkle.ltd
Repo: github.com/rachitsinghi/hcde530/MP2 (also separate repo twinkle-tinker — being consolidated)
What it is: Immersive interactive star map where users draw custom constellations mapped onto real HYG catalog stars

Three input methods:
1. Manual sketch pad — click-click polyline, dot grid, draggable vertices
2. IMAGINE feature — type description → Groq matches to Iconify API → fetches real SVG →
   extracts straight-line path points → plots as draggable vertices
3. Finger drawing — Google MediaPipe Hand Landmarker, index fingertip (landmark 8) tracked;
   calibration step measures palm size and scales threshold adaptively

Core features:
- 8,834 stars rendered with mag → size and ci → color encoding
- MAP TO STARS: each sketch vertex snaps to nearest catalog star (brighter star preferred in ties)
- GET NAME: Groq API (llama-3.1-8b-instant) via Cloudflare Workers edge function generates mythological name
- 2D/3D toggle (Three.js, OrbitControls)
- Download PNG (html2canvas)
- Mobile AR sky view: device orientation (alpha/beta) maps to RA/Dec, rear camera overlay,
  constellation highlighted when in viewport
- Mobile bottom sheet with context-aware collapsed states
- Zoom in/out pill buttons — bottom-left desktop, bottom-right mobile
- PWA support for home screen installation
- Custom domain twinkle.ltd

Tech stack: React 19, TanStack Start, Three.js 0.184, MediaPipe, Groq API, Iconify API,
  Cloudflare Workers, Vite 7, Tailwind CSS 4, shadcn/ui, PapaParse, Python/pandas for data prep

Data pipeline: Week 8/prepare_stars.py — filters HYG to mag < 6.5, removes Sol (dist < 0.01),
  converts RA hours to degrees (ra_deg = ra * 15), computes x/y/z Cartesian, fills missing values,
  outputs stars_visible.csv to MP2/public/

Scope changes from MP2a declaration:
- Supabase persistence cut entirely (no database shipped)
- Freehand curves replaced with straight-line polyline segments
- Export simplified to PNG only

Three AI failures documented in MP2/mp2.md:
1. Groq coordinate generation — LLMs can't do geometry; switched to Iconify SVG parsing
2. Quick Draw CORS — routed through edge function but latency 2–8 seconds; switched to Iconify
3. MediaPipe finger sensitivity — fixed with distance gate (55px) + time gate (400ms) + palm-size calibration

Submission files:
- MP2/README.md — full project documentation
- MP2/mp2.md — competency claims (C6, C7, C8) with specific code references
- MP2/reflection.md — 500-word reflection answering four questions

--- END-OF-QUARTER REFLECTION ---

Files: End-of-Quarter Reflection.md / End-of-Quarter Reflection.pdf (submitted to Canvas)
Full text: see END-OF-QUARTER REFLECTION (FULL TEXT) section below
Three competency domains argued: C5, C7, C8

Three things learned outside objectives:
1. Managing AI as a directed tool not an oracle — "looks complete" and "is correct" are different properties
2. Right representation over impressive representation — chose 2D over 3D for Felis because 2D is correct
   for what a constellation is
3. Silent failures don't produce errors — learned to ask "could this be wrong in a way that would not tell me"

--- KEY DECISIONS AND CONTEXT ---

- Dataset choice: started with three incompatible CSVs; switched to HYG after catching fabricated
  correlations in synthetic merge
- Platform: Lovable for frontend deployment, Cursor for Python data work
- API naming: Groq (free, no credit card) instead of Claude API
- Domain: twinkle.ltd — chosen after long brainstorm (considered Lyracraft, Starweave, Illustar,
  Starling, Stardoodle, Glimmer, Constella)
- App name history: started as TwinkleTinker; went through many iterations
- PWA: added for mobile home screen installation; updates automatically when Lovable publishes

--- LINKEDIN POST (FINAL VERSION — TWINKLE LAUNCH) ---

Spent the last few weeks building something fun — half coding, half vibecoding, and I'm really proud
of how it turned out.

Twinkle is an interactive star map where you draw your own constellation and watch it snap onto 8,834
real stars from NASA's astronomical catalog. Every star is sized by actual brightness and colored by
real stellar temperature — Betelgeuse shows up orange-red, Rigel blue-white, exactly as they look from Earth.

The fun part is how you draw it. Sketch on a pad, type "cat face" and let AI pull a matching shape from
275,000 icons, or wave your finger at your camera and draw in mid-air using Google MediaPipe hand tracking.
Your shape snaps to the nearest real stars, an AI names your constellation, and on mobile you can point
your phone at the actual sky and see it overlaid through the camera.

The whole thing runs on a React frontend talking to a Python-processed star catalog, with Three.js for the
3D view, Groq powering the AI naming, and Lovable and Cursor doing a lot of the heavy lifting on the build
side. The interesting challenge wasn't the code — it was learning when to trust the AI output and when to
throw it out and start over.

Try it: twinkle.ltd

Hashtags: #vibecoding #buildinpublic #cursorai #mediapipe #threejs #designengineer #AItools
#datavisualization #augmentedreality #shipIt #react #creativity

INTRACK — NON-INVASIVE NUTRIENT TRACKING WEARABLE APP
================================================================================
Hackathon project (ZeroToOne Hackathon). Fully interactive React prototype for a wearable health app
that tracks 6 nutrient biomarkers non-invasively in real time.

Live prototype: https://in-track.vercel.app
GitHub: https://github.com/uwmahigvs/InTrack
Figma: https://figma.com/design/Xb2t4qCZI2B7jgBjiHHOqk/Hackathon

Owner: Rachit Singhi, MS Human-Centered Design & Engineering, University of Washington
Portfolio: https://www.rachitsinghidesign.com

CV bullet: "Conceived and prototyped an end-to-end wearable health product concept tracking 6 nutrient
biomarkers, defining the full product architecture — 9-screen onboarding, 3-path user journey system,
AI-powered meal recommendation flow, and teleconsultation booking — and shipped a live interactive
prototype validating the concept at ZeroToOne Hackathon"

Biomarkers tracked (6): Vitamin D, Magnesium, B12, Electrolytes, Hydration, Antioxidants

--- TECH STACK ---

- React 18, single-file component architecture (~1640 lines in intrack-complete.jsx artifact)
- Vite (build tool), deployed on Vercel
- CSS-in-JS inline styles with design tokens
- No external UI libraries — fully custom component system
- Built with Claude Code (vibecoding)

--- DESIGN TOKENS (from Figma node 11:497) ---

- Background: #0D0D0F
- Surface: #161618 | SurfaceHigh: #1E1E23
- Brand teal: #4ECDC4 / #2EA89E
- Text Primary: #F2F2F7 | Text Secondary: #A0A0AB | Text Muted: #5C5C66
- Success: #30D158 | Warning: #FF9F0A | Danger: #FF453A | Info: #0A84FF
- Font: SF Pro Rounded, Inter
- Orb blur: 49.214px | Pill radius: 100.716px
- Glassmorphism: backdrop-filter: blur(20px)

--- APP ARCHITECTURE ---

Onboarding (9 screens):
1. Onb0 — Brand splash (InTrack logo, tagline "Interact. Track. Thrive.", Get Started CTA)
2. Onb1 — Login (Email / Google / Apple)
3. Onb2 — Connect InTrack band (BLE pairing animation)
4. Onb3 — Wear mode (smartwatch vs standalone)
5. Onb4 — Setup guide (OnbQuick stub)
6. Onb5 — Health profile (height, weight, activity, location autocomplete, water target)
7. OnbJourney — Journey selection (3 cards: Supplement, Diet, Hybrid)
8. Onb6 — Blood test upload (optional, skip → lab booking flow)
9. Onb7 — Baseline insights (6 nutrient donut charts)

Main App (5 tabs):
- Home — Alert banner, wearable chip, priority card, meal nudge, nutrient grid (6 Ring progress cards),
  streak card, supplement checklist (journey-conditional)
- Insights — Blood test upload card, nutrient reports, medication tracker with next dose + mark as taken,
  share/export
- Journey — Plan status, journey-conditional content (supplement plan + teleconsult OR dietary changes +
  meal ideas), doing well section, meal suggestion card
- InTrack AI — Multi-turn food ordering conversation with restaurant listings, Order Now buttons,
  DoorDash overlay, 4 single-turn responses
- Profile — Health data, water target, connected devices, journey type selector, streak, notifications,
  privacy, FAQ

--- KEY STATE (AppProvider context) ---

- onbStep (1-9), screen ("onboarding" / "app"), tab
- journeyType: "supplement" | "diet" | "hybrid"
- nutrientScores — live scores updated by food logging
- suppChecks — supplement taken/not, synced between Home and Insights
- uploadDone — blood test uploaded (shows Calibrated vs Estimated badges)
- loggedMeals, streak, deepLink, toasts
- profile (age, sex, height, weight, skinTone, diet, location, activityLevel)

--- JOURNEY TYPE WIRING ---

- Supplement: supplement checklist on Home, supplement plan + teleconsult on Journey, supplement AI suggestions
- Diet: hides supplement checklist, dietary changes + weekly meal ideas on Journey, diet AI suggestions,
  food-focused top action
- Hybrid: combines both journeys — all checklist/plan/meal content + hybrid AI suggestions

--- INTRACK AI TAB — MULTI-TURN FOOD ORDERING FLOW ---

1. "I want to order food for dinner" → nutrient analysis → chips (Yes suggest / specific mood)
2. → Grilled Salmon Bowl recommendation with full nutrient breakdown
3. → Order from DoorDash / Whole Foods chips
4. → Restaurant list (Sweetgreen $16.95, Chipotle $14.50, Tender Greens $18.75) with Order Now buttons
5. → Order Now tapped → 2s overlay "Opening DoorDash..." → toast → follow-up with projected score improvements

Alternate path: cuisine selection (Italian/Asian/Mexican/Mediterranean) → tailored meal recommendation
Single-turn responses for: Vitamin D foods, Magnesium dropping explanation, weekly summary

--- ICON SYSTEM ---

- const Ic — 24+ filled SVG icons (Home, Bar, Compass, Person, Back, Check, X, Alert, Walk, Fork, Pill,
  Doc, Share, PDF, Plus, Target, Lab, Sun, Drop, Leaf, Bolt, Crystal, Flask, Camera, SearchIc, Clock,
  Mail, Google, Apple, Moon, Breakfast, Dinner, Heart, Flame, Spark, Upload, ChevD, ChevU)
- const NutIcon — lookup: {vitd:Ic.Sun, mag:Ic.Crystal, b12:Ic.Bolt, elec:Ic.Flask, hydra:Ic.Drop, antio:Ic.Leaf}
- All icons filled/solid only; active/inactive differentiated by color only

--- CRITICAL RENDERER CONSTRAINTS (for AI/code generation) ---

1. No JSX fragments (<>...</>) — replace with <div> or <g> (SVG)
2. No IIFEs with hooks — extract to named components
3. Extracted component: NutrientDetailPanel (from InsightsTab detail view)

--- COMPONENT STRUCTURE ---

- GBtn — glass button (variants: primary/secondary/ghost/danger/success; multiple sizes)
- Card — surface card with optional accent border
- Bdg — status badge pill
- Ring — animated SVG progress ring
- Spark — sparkline chart
- LineChart — interactive line chart with hover tooltip
- OnbLayout — onboarding wrapper (back button + step counter; no dots in top bar)
- ProgressDots — standalone above each CTA in onboarding
- OnbScreen — fade/slide transition wrapper
- FAB — floating action button (Home tab only; if tab!=="home" return null)
- FoodSheet — spring bottom sheet for meal logging
- Toasts — toast notification system
- Orbs — background gradient orb system per tab
- StatusBar — live clock
- BottomNav — 5-tab navigation

--- KNOWN PREVIOUS ISSUES (fixed) ---

- JSX fragment </> in FoodSheet options phase — fixed to </div>
- Smart curly quotes causing Babel parse errors — replaced with straight quotes
- Duplicate else if in Profile journey toggle — cleaned up
- hasSup/hasDiet variable leak from "both" experiment — reverted to isSup/isDiet

--- GENERATED ARTIFACTS (prototype build session) ---

- intrack-complete.jsx — single-file React artifact (~142K chars, ~1640 lines)
- 23 full-screen HD screenshots at 3x retina (screens/)
- 43 individual element screenshots (elements/)
- InTrack-Case-Study.docx — full technical case study
- intrack-vercel-deploy.zip — Vite project ready for deployment

ABOUT RACHIT — NARRATIVE
================================================================================

Origin story:
How can I question normality and imagine the "What if?" This curiosity led Rachit to study industrial design at the National Institute of Design (NID), where he started with physical products — in the field, observing users, and designing for real-world constraints where failure was more than just theoretical.

Transition to digital:
Over time, he was drawn to digital systems. Somewhere between interviews, systems maps, and more Figma files than he can count, he realized what makes him tick: turning ambiguity and users' doubt into clarity. He designs in the messy middle, where user needs, business goals, and real-world constraints collide.

What he loves:
- Talking to users and collaborating with people
- Mapping workflows and catching the quiet assumptions hiding inside them
- Sketching early and sharing before things feel "ready" — not because critique is "part of the process" but because it makes the outcome better

What excites him:
- Simplifying complex workflows and systems
- AI-integrated products and leveraging emerging technologies
- Bridging research insights with production-ready execution
- Building scalable design systems and languages

Open to connect:
"If you're building thoughtful products or navigating messy design challenges (or just want to vent about bad interfaces), I'm always up for a conversation."

Research Scholar Intern | Thinkonomers (HDL)
May 2021 – June 2021
- 25+ user interviews and observations informed design recommendations that shaped stakeholder decisions around improving aural hygiene routines

--- PROJECT 1: Dashboard for Agricultural Transformation ---
URL: https://www.rachitsinghidesign.com/mathematica
Year: 2024
Tags: User Research | Systems Thinking | Rapid User Testing | UX/UI Design
Impact metrics:
- 300+ everyday users
- 11+ African countries rely on it

Summary:
We partnered with Mathematica and AGRA to build a dashboard tracking agrarian transformation across Africa, turning complex data into an intuitive tool for informed decision-making.

Overview:
Mathematica, a leader in evidence-based research and data analysis, partnered with AGRA, a non-profit driving agricultural transformation in Africa, to create a data dashboard for tracking progress across countries. They asked us to design this dashboard, transforming complex, multi-source datasets into a clear, intuitive tool for decision-making. AGRA leaders, from country directors to VPs, would use it to assess progress, identify gaps, and compare results by country and crop during quarterly and annual planning.

Rachit's role:
Involved from inception to completion. Led efforts to organize and interpret scattered data, explore effective visualization approaches, and manage testing, refinement, and final handover. Collaborated closely with team for feedback; developed strong ownership and deepened understanding of data visualization, both technically and strategically.

Discovery — Secondary research:
01. Understanding R Shiny's capabilities — explored R Shiny's potential for interactive, data-driven dashboards suited to AGRA's scale; reviewed case studies and documentation.
02. Researching effective data visualization methods — analyzed best practices and existing dashboards across sectors for agricultural indicators.

Discovery — User research:
Main challenge: AGRA's complex, multi-variable dataset spanning regions and time periods. Conducted semi-structured interviews with two stakeholders from each team to understand workflows, reporting expectations, and decision-making needs.

Key insights:
- Simplicity was crucial — at-a-glance insights without overwhelming data
- Comparisons were key — track progress across countries, crops, and variables
- Customization mattered — different teams needed tailored views

Design — Ideation tradeoffs:
- Clarity vs visual appeal — simplicity prioritized over visual complexity
- Scalability vs detail — some graph types hard to maintain as dataset grew
- Consistency vs experimentation — micro visualizations needed greater consistency with detailed charts

Design approach:
- Flexible Layout — modular, scalable framework for future data additions
- User-Friendly Navigation — seamless navigation with clear place-awareness
- Micro-visualizations — glanceable charts with filters and drill-downs

Development:
High-level summary on landing page; micro-visualizations with hover/click details; consistency in color, navigation, visual hierarchy; grouped bar and line graphs tailored for clarity, comparisons, and trend detection. UX guidelines documented for future iterations and technical scalability.

Testing:
Tested graph and visualization types. Customized user flows for country heads, business line leaders, and senior management.

Success criteria — users could:
- Navigate the dashboard independently
- Locate information efficiently
- Interpret visualizations correctly
- Drill down into relevant data
- Compare information across datasets
- Answer reporting questions with confidence

Improvements identified:
- Customizability for personalized dashboards
- Specific drill-downs with additional filters and comparison tools

Handoff:
Worked closely with development team for feasibility within technical constraints. Ensured R Shiny compatibility. Accounted for no-data, zero states, active states, and all interaction scenarios. Built for scalability via modular layouts and design system.

Challenges:
- Balancing diverse stakeholder needs
- Cross-continental collaboration (US, Africa, India) — time zones, languages, workflows
- Technical limitations in development software — trade-offs between design intent and implementation

Reflections:
01. Functionality over aesthetics — aligning dashboard with user workflows more impactful than visual embellishments
02. Designing for clarity — simplifying multi-country datasets into actionable visuals influences better, faster decision-making
03. Collaborative cooperation — design became the universal language bridging geographic and stakeholder differences

Mentor: Prof. Amit Jena (Faculty of Design, Art & Performance) — see Testimonials section.

--- PROJECT 2: Tool for Chatbot Customization (InSync.AI) ---
URL: https://www.rachitsinghidesign.com/insync
Year: 2025
Tags: User Research | Systems Thinking | UI Design
Impact metrics:
- 3× faster chatbot deployment
- 40% reduction in support costs
Timeline note: Designed in a two-week sprint

Summary:
InSync.AI helps enterprises launch smart, no-code chatbots fast. We designed their builder to be intuitive, powerful, and scalable.

Overview:
InSync.AI is a Conversational AI platform helping enterprises deploy intelligent chatbots across customer support, e-commerce, and education. Partnered to design a no-code configuration platform enabling users to create and customize chatbots effortlessly. Goal: simplify a traditionally technical process — configure chatbot behavior, tone, and integrations through an intuitive interface. Designed for first-time users and enterprise power users; reduces development dependency and accelerates deployment.

Rachit's role:
Responsible for understanding all stages/features in the complete user flow and creating the final product from scratch based on requirements. Translated wireframes into cohesive visual system; refined interactions for clarity and scalability; led end-to-end design. Managed developer handoff with design logic, interaction behavior, and UI guidelines.

Discovery — Design principles:
- Semantic Intuition — interfaces feel familiar; quick decisions
- Clarity Over Complexity — easy navigation; minimal overwhelm
- SaaS Meets Simplicity — industrial SaaS functionality with modern minimal aesthetic despite being a backend solution

Mapped core user flows; structured sprint around clusters of related features for rapid prototyping with cohesion.

Design — Development highlights:
01. Clear and Confident UX — placeholder text, microcopy, smart defaults; reduced tooltip overuse
02. Building for Flexibility & Scale — modular UI system with reusable components for MVP and growth
03. Navigation That Mirrors Real-World Use — grouped tasks mirroring customer success onboarding flows

Testing & iteration:
- Replaced top progress bar with left-side navigation panel (flexibility, perceived control)
- Replaced lengthy text with info icons and ghost text (reduced cognitive load)
- Restructured into modular framework with clear visual hierarchy (scalability)

Handoff:
Modular UI system and reusable components shared. Cross-functional alignment with dev teams on prototype and component logic. Comprehensive UX documentation with rationale and behavioral guidelines.

Challenges:
- Grasping every stage of chatbot creation process initially
- Building modular system for MVP that could expand without overcomplicating first release
- Turning technical configurations into intuitive guided experience — multiple iterations

Reflections:
01. Design Systems are Strategic — drive scalability and team alignment, not just visual consistency
02. Small Interactions Matter — ghost text and info icons make complex workflows feel effortless
03. Collaboration Builds Clarity — shared understanding turns design intent into impact

Status (as of 2025 on site): Product in active development; future iterations rolling out based on early user learnings.

--- PROJECT 3: Optimizing Candidate Communications (Teach For India) ---
URL: https://www.rachitsinghidesign.com/teach-for-india
Year: 2024
Tags: User Research | Systems Thinking | Communication Strategy | Graphic Design
Impact metrics:
- 52% reduction in manual communications
- 22% reduction in channels of communications

Summary:
We partnered with Teach For India to streamline recruitment communications, making candidate experiences more efficient, consistent, and personal.

Overview:
Teach For India is a non-profit working to end educational inequity through its nationwide Fellowship program. Partnered to streamline and enhance recruitment communications — simplify a complex, largely manual process into a unified, efficient, engaging system delivering the right message at the right time. Balances automation with personalization; reduces recruiter workload; ensures consistency; strengthens candidate experience.

Rachit's role:
Joined as designer. Developed user flow and mapped end-to-end candidate journey through Service Blueprint. Led ideation and refinement of blueprinting approach, development, and templatization of key communication collaterals. Contributed to data analysis and insight synthesis with project lead. Independently executed all graphic design work. Highly collaborative with clearly defined roles.

Discovery — Wisdom Mining Workshop (2 days):
01. Introductions — all recruitment teams shared roles and candidate interactions; built empathy; surfaced interdependencies
02. Personas — Naina (recent graduate exploring meaningful career) and Varun (working professional seeking impact)
03. Open-Ended Problem Statement — reframed challenges into open questions for human-centered communication
04. Hits, Misses, and Things to Start Doing — evaluated each recruitment stage for friction and automation opportunities

Also analyzed recruitment data: application highs/lows, drop-off points, candidate feedback.

User interview findings:
- Diverse candidates (students vs professionals) need tailored communication strategies
- Teams valued unified messaging across platforms for consistent, inspiring narrative
- Tone/quality variations across channels (especially social media) fragmented brand experience

Problem diagnosis:
Root problem: absence of a unified system — inconsistent, visually fragmented, manually intensive messaging. Audited 200+ content pieces (emails to social posts) using five criteria: visuals, relevance, structure, conciseness, tone. Built scoring matrix with benchmarks.

Scale & flexibility:
Redesigned key emails for Gmail templates; refined through RITE testing with real candidates. Templating even 10% of materials improved efficiency and consistency without losing personalization.

Service Blueprint:
Detailed blueprint of every stage/substage, touchpoints, front-stage and backstage actions, supporting processes, collateral. Found 40% of routine touchpoints (intros, reminders, follow-ups) could be automated. Mapped manual, automated, and semi-automated interactions with distinct line styles; color-coded props and people.

Ecosystem Map:
Mapped communication hotspots; exposed duplication (multiple email IDs); highlighted channel consolidation opportunities.

Structural transformation:
8 root challenges identified (timing misalignment to redundant workflows). Prioritization matrix → phased roadmap focusing on highest-impact changes first.

Key learnings:
01. Inconsistency weakens trust — shifting tone across email, WhatsApp, social media diluted mission
02. Disjointed social media limits impact — inconsistent visual identity hurt engagement and recall
03. Manual tasks strain team capacity — automating 40% of repetitive communication could boost productivity
04. Scattered ownership causes confusion — centralized guidelines and accountability improved experience

Handoff & Workshop:
Training workshop with three activities:
- Activity 1: Service Blueprint Mapping — solved blueprint puzzle
- Activity 2: Professional Email Writing — designed email/WhatsApp invites using templates
- Activity 3: Communication Collateral Design — matched collaterals to correct service stages

Challenges:
- Organizing scattered data across hundreds of communication pieces
- Balancing structure with empathy — standardizing without losing human tone
- Collaborating across diverse stakeholders — communicating clearly and thinking systemically

Reflections:
01. Structured Collaboration — shared ownership through workshops and blueprints creates alignment faster than endless discussion
02. People Over Processes — communication design is about how information feels, not just consistency
03. Comfort in Uncertainty — early messiness taught openness, fast experimentation, trust in iteration

--- Research Paper ---
Title: A Mix Method Approach to Study the Effect of Touch on Self-identity
Date: 26th October, 2025
Venue: Responsible and Resilient Design for Society, Volume 11
Conference: International Conference on Research into Design (ICoRD'25) — paper selected for presentation
Full paper link: https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1007/978-981-96-6414-6_14
Read time listed: 45 min read

Abstract (from site):
This study examines how touch influences self-identity, trauma, and personality development. Through interviews and visual methods (n=15), it revealed the impact of gender bias, social norms, and gaps in early education. The insights informed the design of an educational activity kit for children (ages 8–13) that teaches boundaries and emotional awareness.

Co-authorship noted in Dr. Shikha Agarwal testimonial: "A Mixed Method Approach to Study the Effect of Touch on Self-Identity"

--- LinkedIn Post (featured on site) ---
Date: 15th May, 2025
Title: Design for now, sure — but also for what's next.
Author/context: BRND Studio post featuring Rachit's design thinking
Link: https://www.linkedin.com/posts/brndstudio_design-for-now-but-also-for-whats-next-activity-7330449734320500736-HDEn
Read time: 1.5 min read

Summary:
Well-designed screens often look complete until product scope expands, exposing cracks when new data, features, or use cases are introduced. Scalable design is about anticipating growth through flexible layouts, strong foundations, and systems that adapt gracefully, so products can evolve without constant redesign.

Key themes from full post:
- Products grow and evolve; designs must keep up without full redesigns each time
- Scalability = flexible layouts, empty states, edge cases, overflow readiness, nav structure that holds as pages grow
- Strong foundations (spacing, color, typography) help design scale, not stretch
- Key question: "If this product had 10x more cards tomorrow, would it still work?"
- Tags: #UXDesign #ScalableDesign #DesignSystems #ProductDesign #Figma #DesignThinking

PRATT
-
MS
in
Information
Experience
Design

Requirements
-
A statement of purpose (no more than 500 words) describing long-range goals and interest in the chosen
discipline and reason for applying to the program. The Admissions Committee views the statement of purpose
as a means of gauging an applicant’s fit in the program, how intellectually curious they are about the world
around them, and how they’d contribute to the diversity of the student population at the School of
Information. The statement is also a way for the Committee to learn more about an applicant beyond what is
indicated on a resume or transcript. Please tell us why you believe the program is right for you and how/why
it aligns with your long-term goals and professional aspirations. Please do not include details that can be found
in
your
resume.

SOP
Growing up in Bangalore, life unfolded in straight lines and stark edges, where every structure was a servant of
purpose, and aesthetics took a backseat to utility. It wasn’t until I wandered through the vibrant streets of
Barcelona, for a trip during high school, that I discovered the quiet poetry of aesthetics in public spaces. This
revelation stirred a deep admiration within me during those early years. My undergraduate studies in Industrial
Design and diverse professional experiences have shaped my ensuing creative practice. During this time, I have
explored the design process in areas like innovative product development, user-centric methodologies, and
systems thinking. This ability to use scientific advancements to create new products and services that drive
business and economy while making people’s lives easier and more comfortable excites and motivates me to
build a long-term career in this field. I now wish to augment my portfolio and train my design thinking mindset
to scope, refine, and deliver practicable solutions and translate abstract ideas, theories, and plans into practice
through an MS in Information Experience Design.
This academic goal is a well-thought-out progression of my interests and skillset. I have always loved arts and
crafts as a young boy and knew that I wanted to work in a field that would allow me to express my creativity and
challenge me intellectually. My Bachelor’s degree from India’s premier design school National Institute of Design
(NID), has given my design thought, creativity, and critical thinking a decisively humane and people-oriented
direction.  It introduced me to three facets of design: systems design, service design, and interaction design –
each with its unique applications that called for deeper exploration. The systems approach calls for looking at a
problem area holistically before identifying an intervention type, service design relies on solving design problems
with the aid of techno-digital interventions, whereas interaction designs shed light on making such designs more
user-centric.
From developing a mechanical tool for garland weaving that improved the efficiency and comfort of flower
vendors to creating an educational activity kit exploring self-identity for children, (the latter is selected for
presentation and publication at the International Conference on Research into Design - ICoRD’25), all my
projects
have
reiterated
the
interconnection
of
design,
community,
and
sustainability.

Collectively, these five years of formative learning have coalesced into my chosen career path in  Information
Experience Design. After graduate studies, I plan to work as a UX Researcher or Innovation Strategist with
creative firms like Google, Huge Inc., or Siemens Healthcare, on projects that blend strategy, design, and
technology. Specifically, I aim to work on service ecosystems that address pressing socio-economic inequities by
co-creating accessible services for marginalized communities - such as affordable healthcare frameworks or skill-
building digital platforms for rural artisans, inspired by my earlier work in Assam. I am also open to working on
digital products like fintech solutions, or interactive educational platforms.  My long-term vision is to become an
expert in human-centric design by creating versatile design solutions that have high utility, speak to the
audience, and help achieve the underlying business objectives.


--- Page 2 ---
The Information Experience Design program at Pratt Institute is the perfect conduit to materialize these. I am
particularly interested in the Practical Ethnography for User Experience, Speculative Design, and Information
Architecture modules which encourage design thinking and conversance with industry-relevant tools. Pratt’s
emphasis on practical learning through industry collaborations, and live projects, and its state-of-the-art UX labs
like the semantic lab and observation room provide an ideal environment for me to experiment with emerging
technologies such as Usability Machines. I am excited to collaborate with the intellectually spirited student
cohort for international study opportunities and engage in team-based innovation to devise solutions for
contemporary social and environmental challenges. By making full use of these and the numerous other
opportunities on campus, I do not doubt that I will become an industry-ready professional, possessing the skills
I need to achieve my goals.

teaching tools. These experiences have amalgamated into my own design philosophy, based on creating

Why do you want to attend SCAD? * (250 words max)

Through my undergraduate study of Industrial Design, and field experience, I have explored the design
process in areas like innovative product development, user-centric methodologies, and systems
thinking. This ability to use scientific advancements to create new products and services that drive
business and economy and at the same time make people’s lives easier and more comfortable is
something that excites and motivates me to build a long-term career in this field. The MA in Service
Design from SCAD will sharpen my design thinking mindset to refine and deliver practicable solutions
and translate abstract ideas, theories and plans into practice.

I am particularly interested in the Mixed Methods Research, Visualizing Services, and Systemic
Innovation for Service Evolution modules which encourage design thinking and conversance with
industry relevant tools. SCAD’s emphasis on practical learning through industry collaborations, live
projects, and its state-of-the-art Gulfstream Center, model shop, and Computer labs provide an ideal
environment for me to experiment with emerging technologies such as AR/VR and Immersive media.
I am also excited at the prospect of collaborating with the intellectually spirited student cohort for the
SCAD Challenge and engage in team-based innovation for SCAD SERVE and its Design for Good
courses where students work pro-bono for NPOs to devise solutions for contemporary social and
environmental challenges.

By making full use of these and the numerous other opportunities on campus, I have no doubt that I
will become an industry-ready professional, possessing the skills I need to achieve my goals.


Who is your favorite artist/designer and why? 250 word max

Amongst pioneers of human-centered service design, Steve Krug’s seminal work, Don’t Make Me
Think, has profoundly shaped my understanding of design. His philosophy is radical in its simplicity: he
emphasizes usability principles such as clear hierarchies and intuitive pathways. In other words, good
service design ensures that interactions—both digital and physical—are as effortless as possible.

But like all novice designers, I too initially focused on surface-level requirements and aesthetic designs.
Over time, through practice and feedback (and some humbling mistakes!), I realized the importance
of going to the root of user needs, reducing fluff and making designs that work so well that they
become almost invisible to the user.

I was fortunate to find a mentor who shares these values—Mr. Sudhir Bhatia, the founder of BRND,
my current studio. He often says that a well-designed system is like a well-oiled machine; it may not
always be aesthetically beautiful, but it operates smoothly, ensuring that every interaction contributes
to a cohesive and effective experience. Working with him has reinforced my belief that service design
is not just about optimizing interfaces but orchestrating entire systems to serve people better.

While I do not have an absolute favorite, Krug’s teachings and Bhatia’s mentorship have made a
significant impact on my design ethos. By studying their work and integrating their techniques into my


--- Page 6 ---
design process, I hope to create functional products and services that reduce cognitive load, and
ultimately enhance the lives of those who interact with them.


How will your life and/or professional experience impact your ability to succeed at SCAD? 250 word
max

During the past five years of immersion in the field of design, I have developed a strong foundation in
user-centered research, participatory design, behavioral mapping, and service innovation. From
redesigning construction barricades, creating an educational activity kit to teach children about
personal boundaries, developing a mechanical tool for flower vendors, to promoting a dying
indigenous, bamboo art form from Assam, my academic research has given me an acute EQ approach
to empathize with diverse user groups and develop practical, impactful solutions for sensitive and
high-impact domains—an essential skill for tackling real-world service challenges I will encounter in
the practicum-based teaching-learning environment of SCAD.

On the technical skills front, I have experience in behavioral mapping and iterative prototyping.
Moreover, my UX/UI design experience, my work at Thinkonomers (HDL), Pichkaari Design Studio, and
BRND Studio has given me a trans-disciplinary and versatile skillset, enabling me to effectively navigate
my graduate coursework in service blueprinting and systems thinking.

My dual exposure to traditional rebranding as well as tech-intensive design processes and tools has
amalgamated into my own design philosophy based on creating superlative experiences for both
virtual and real spaces. Personally, leading multi-industry and multicultural projects has made me
comfortable with ambiguity and iterative problem-solving, both of which are at the crux of service
design. Lastly, I believe my passion for accessibility and inclusion also mirror SCAD’s own values and
ethos of diversity and will enable me to contribute meaningfully to its collaborative studio projects.

enhancing user experience in digital platforms I have learned how to bridge the gap between design
theory and real-world implementation. Being a proactive learner, I have amplified my classroom study

I believe my success as a service designer stems from my result-oriented mindset and iterative

--- Page 7 ---
sectors, demonstrate my ability to integrate strategic thinking with creative execution. These skills

In essence, my academic performance, hands-on experience in service and interaction design, and my

Statement of Purpose? 500-750 word max
Your statement should give an overview of your academic and personal experience, describing
preparation for and commitment to further study at SCAD, as well as educational and professional
aspirations.

Growing up in Bangalore, life unfolded in straight lines and stark edges, where every structure was a
servant of purpose, and aesthetics took a backseat to utility. It wasn’t until I wandered through the
vibrant streets of Barcelona, for a trip during high school, that I discovered the quiet poetry of
aesthetics in public spaces. This revelation stirred a deep admiration within me during those early
years. My ensuing creative practice has been shaped by my undergraduate studies in Industrial Design
and diverse professional experiences.

As I took on curricular assignments to apply classroom theories in realtime practice, I gradually
identified my design niche. For my graduation assignment with Grant Thornton, I worked with
indigenous bamboo artisans from Assam to revive endangered Japi crafts and saw firsthand how
design had the unique power to effect social change. For a similar project, by using a participatory
design approach, I designed a mechanical tool that alleviated the physical strain and increased the
productivity of flower vendors engaged in garland weaving activities. I also used behavioral mapping
to understand the challenges faced by pedestrians and drivers, designed a lightweight, highly visible
construction barricade to improve safety for pedestrians during peak traffic hours.

Beyond these community-based projects, I worked on two tech-intensive projects. In the first, I
analyzed STI management practices and barriers restricting access to services among female sex
workers (FSWs) in Bhopal. Employing snowball sampling techniques to locate their work zones and,
using methods like GIGA mapping user journeys, I developed a Trigger and Response Model to better
interpret the data. The project led to recommendations for community-centric support systems such
as mobile clinics and awareness programs. In the second project I created an educational activity kit
to help children explore self-identity. By utilizing user journey mapping, participatory testing, and
iterative prototyping, I built a tool to help children understand and express their feelings, which was
later presented and published at the International Conference on Research into Design (ICoRD’25).

From a bird’s eye perspective, all my projects have reiterated the interconnection of design, utility,
and sustainability. This understanding has been further strengthened through my professional
experiences - at Thinkonomers (HDL) where I learned about the importance of user feedback in the
design process, Pichkaari Design Studio, where I worked on rebranding projects and developed user
flow enhancement prototypes, Grant Thornton, and finally in my current role as a UX/UI designer at


--- Page 8 ---
BRND Studio, where I handle end-to-end design for SaaS dashboards, educational platforms, and
teaching tools. These experiences have ingrained in me that user experience should be the top priority
in the design process and helped shape my own design philosophy, which is based on creating
superlative, easy to use experiences for modern spaces, both virtual and real. For example, in my initial
projects, I dove headfirst into design but with experience and trial and error, I realised that logic in
design will hold little value unless it is thoughtfully integrated with an intuitive understanding of how
it will be used by humans.

Collectively, these five years of formative learnings have coalesced into my chosen career path in
Service Design. After graduate studies, I plan to work as a Service Designer or Innovation Strategist
with creative firms like Adobe or Deloitte, on projects that blend strategy, design, and technology. I
am passionate about working on service ecosystems that address critical challenges in accessibility,
equity, and inclusion for underserved populations.  For example, I want to design services for
marginalized communities, such as affordable healthcare frameworks or digital platforms for skilling
and business training for rural and tribal artisans. These goals are inspired by my earlier project in
Assam, where I worked with artisans to develop community-driven solutions. Additionally, I am open
to contributing to digital products like fintech solutions or interactive educational platforms, using my
design background to create user-friendly, impactful tools. My long-term vision is to become an expert
in human-centric design by creating versatile design solutions that have high utility, speak to the
audience, and help achieve the underlying business objectives.

I have come to appreciate that product design albeit a creative process, requires conversance with
software design tools, user-centric methodologies, and an allied understanding of socio-economic
dynamics and business management to truly understand the consumer ask. While I have been working
on developing the aforementioned proficiencies, I require advanced training and international
exposure to the field which I hope to gain through the MA Service Design at SCAD.

Q1. Tell us about someone you look up to and why. The person can be a designer, a friend,
a relative, someone in your neighborhood—anyone who inspires you and your creative
practice.

Q2. Imagine it is 20 years from the present moment. Describe your life—what kind of
work are you engaging in, what are your home and community like, in what ways have
you shaped the field of interaction design, and how has the field of interaction design
shaped your life?

Q3. MFA Interaction Design offers modest, merit-based scholarships. Please indicate in
your essay if you would like to be considered for a merit-based departmental award.


Amongst stalwarts of user-centered design, the person who inspires me most is Steve Krug.
His seminal work Don’t Make Me Think, a book on web usability, has profoundly shaped my
understanding of design. Krug is a radical in a way, emphasizing function over aesthetics,
advocating for self-evident designs that prioritize user experience above all else. What I read
this as, is that, good design should simplify, not complicate. Krug does this by focusing on
clear visual hierarchies and ensuring navigation serves its purpose. I have adapted this idea to
my own work believing that a product’s experience holds more value and precedence over
visual interface. Like all novice designers, I too initially focused on surface-level requirements,
jumping straight into creating the best aesthetic designs I could. But over time, through practice
and feedback (and some humbling mistakes!), I realized the importance of going to the root of
user needs, reducing fluff and making designs that embody clarity —an approach Krug
champions.


--- Page 10 ---

I was searching for like-minded professionals who shared this philosophy and have been
fortunate to work with Mr. Sudhir Bhatia, the founder of _____- my current studio. His
emphasis on experience-driven design has reiterated that a design is like a well-oiled machine,
although at times unpleasant to the eye form the outside, it works smooth as butter on the inside,
fulfilling its intrinsic purpose. Working with him has allowed me to stay true to these principles,
reaffirming that thoughtful, user-centered design is at the heart of innovation.

While I do not have an absolute favorite, Krug’s teachings and Bhatia’s mentorship has made
a significant impact on my personal values and design ethos. By studying their work and
integrating their techniques into my design process, I hope to create functional and intuitive
products and services.

I envision future Designer Rachit, working on ideas that blend strategy, design, and technology,
becoming an expert in human-centric design by creating versatile design solutions that have
high utility, speak to the audience, and help achieve the underlying business objectives. My
collaboration with bamboo artisans in Assam, to help promote the endangered Japi craft, has
shown me how design can breathe new life into traditional art forms. In the future, I see myself
creating modular, self-sustaining products and services like furniture with IoT sensors to
monitor air quality or crosswalks that adjust automatically to ensure the safety of pedestrians
during peak hours. Although this may sound utopian, with the right mix of practicality and
technology, it can become a blueprint for a better future.

In preparation for such a lofty career progression, I have earned a bachelor’s degree from
India’s premier design school National Institute of Design (NID).  I have worked on innovative
projects like redesigning construction barricades, creating an educational activity kit to teach
children about personal boundaries, developing a mechanical tool for flower vendors, to
promoting a dying indigenous, bamboo art form from Assam. I have also challenged myself by
undertaking industry internships to learn the real-world applicability of my studies. At
Thinkonomers (HDL), I learned to apply user feedback in the design process; my work with
Pichkaari Design Studio, revolved around rebranding projects and developing user flow
enhancement prototypes; at Grant Thornton, I undertook a community-driven design project to
revive endangered Japi craft of Assam; and finally, in my current role as a UX/UI designer at
BRND Studio, I handle end-to-end design for SaaS dashboards, educational platforms, and
teaching tools.

In addition to my academic and professional pursuits, I have actively participated in various
extracurricular activities that have refined my teamwork and leadership and given me a well-
rounded skillset that I believe will enable me to perform at my best during my Masters.

It has been an incredible journey these past few years and I am now excited to savor every
experience of graduate life, whether it is the rigorous course curriculum, access to the SVA
alumni network, or the prospect of living in NYC. As an independent individual, I would
appreciate your feedback on my candidacy and kindly request you to consider any merit-based


--- Page 11 ---
scholarship that may be available. would not only ease my financial situation but also allow
me to fully devote myself to my studies and actively contribute to the university community. I
bring with me a diverse set of experiences, skills, and perspectives that I believe would greatly
enrich the SVA’s student body. I am deeply passionate about learning, committed to academic
excellence, and eager to make a positive impact both inside and outside the classroom.

I’m Rachit Singhi, an industrial designer with a passion for creating thoughtful, impactful
design experiences and solutions.

Growing up in Bangalore, I was surrounded by residential and corporate complexes with more
focus on utility than aesthetics. Conversely, when I visited heritage places in India or Europe,
I saw there was also a strong element of visuals to each structure. As I undertook design
assignments during undergraduate studies, I discovered art also had the power to effect social
change - whether it’s creating tools to support underserved communities or designing products
that improve daily experiences. One project that deeply shaped my perspective was my work
with indigenous bamboo artisans from Assam to revive the endangered Japi craft. This
experience reinforced my belief that that design doesn’t just change environments—it has the
power to effect social change. But this process requires deep research and analysis of the user’s
ecosystem, along with careful attention to where the most impactful changes can happen.

This has seeded my own design philosophy - for me, interaction design is not just about
aesthetics or functionality—it’s about weaving empathy, creativity, and systemic thinking into
my solutions. I believe good design should empower users while addressing larger societal
needs. With technology and design evolving at breakneck speed, ensuring accessibility to
diverse populations is more important than ever. I’m thus excited to bring my passion for
impactful, user-centered solutions and my drive for interdisciplinary innovation to the next
chapter of my journey—and I can’t wait to share that with you at SVA!

Growing up in Bangalore, life unfolded in straight lines and stark edges, where every structure was a
servant of purpose, and aesthetics took a backseat to utility. It wasn’t until I wandered through the vibrant
streets of Rajasthan, on a trip during high school, that I discovered the quiet poetry of aesthetics in public

a degree in design for my undergraduate education.
As I took on design assignments in college, I increasingly saw that it also had the unique power to effect
social change. What reinforced this was my on-site graduation project in collaboration with Grant
Thornton, where I worked with the indigenous bamboo artisans from Assam to revive the endangered
practice of crafting a Japi. Immersing myself in the local culture deepened my understanding of
community-driven design and the impact it can have on the artisan as well as the customer. From
redesigning construction barricades, creating an educational activity kit that educates children about
personal boundaries, to developing a mechanical tool for flower vendors, my undergraduate studies in
Industrial Design have reiterated the interconnection of design and community. This understanding has
been further strengthened through my professional experiences at Thinkonomers (HDL), where I learned
about the importance of user feedback in the design process; Pichkaari Design Studio, where I worked on
rebranding projects and developed user flow enhancement prototypes; Grant Thornton; and finally, in my
current role as a UX/UI designer at BRND Studio, where I handle end-to-end design for SaaS dashboards,
educational platforms, and teaching tools. These experiences have helped shape my own design
philosophy, which is based on creating superlative experiences for modern spaces, both virtual and real.
This has coalesced into my chosen career path in Service Design. After graduate studies, I plan to work as
a Service Designer or Innovation Strategist with creative firms like IDEO, Fjord, or Deloitte Digital, on
projects that blend strategy, design, and technology. My long-term vision is to become an expert in
human-centric design by creating versatile design solutions that have high utility, speak to the audience,

interested in the Design Futures and Collaborative Unit modules, which encourage design thinking and
conversance with industry-relevant tools. UAL’s emphasis on practical learning through industry

Digital Space provide an ideal environment for me to experiment with emerging technologies such as VR
and machine learning. I am excited to collaborate with the intellectually spirited student cohort for the

■ Choose 1 project from your portfolio and explain how it challenged you and your

Script:

I am Rachit Singhi, a user-centered industrial designer passionate about creating thoughtful, impactful
design experiences and solutions. With the same motive in mind, I undertook a project as a summer
trainee with Grant Thornton Bharat. This corporation provides services to business sectors, such as
accounting and auditing.

One such service the organization works on involves collaborating with multiple rural sector
stakeholders as part of its corporate social responsibility program. I had the opportunity to work at the
organization as a designer for my graduation project, where I collaborated with the bamboo artisans of
Assam (an economically backward state in India) for six months, understanding their craft techniques
and developing two product ranges that appealed to the current market, thereby increasing the income
levels of the artisans. However, the program had several loopholes that I discovered within the first
month.



Considering I wasn’t the first to conduct such training with the artisans, it raised an important question:
Why had previous training sessions not been effective? This question opened a can of worms, allowing
me to examine the entire project holistically. I began questioning whether simply having an output that
the organization thinks is impactful was enough or if it was far more important to consider how to
deliver the output to maximize its impact, considering what the key stakeholders are looking for from
such interventions and training.

This project became a lens through which I understood the importance of service design. It highlighted
the importance of not coming up with a solution for the identified problem area until proper research
has been undertaken with the primary players involved in the ecosystem. Instead of taking a top-down
approach of training deployment, I took a bottom-up approach of doing training needs assessment and
customized the training delivery by getting more native (dialect) speakers on board. This project
highlighted the idea that just having a particular solution isn’t sufficient; rather, how the intervention is
delivered can make all the difference in achieving a meaningful impact that sticks and is applied in a
real-world scenario.

University of Washington - Personal Statement 01

How have your prior activities and experiences (e.g., things you have done at school, in the
workplace, in your community, and/or extracurricular activities) prepared you for this
program and this field? Please provide specific examples. [600 words maximum]

Growing up in Bangalore, life unfolded in straight lines and stark edges, where every structure
was a servant of purpose, and aesthetics took a backseat to utility. It wasn’t until I wandered
through the vibrant streets of Barcelona, for a trip during high school, that I discovered the
quiet poetry of aesthetics in public spaces. This revelation stirred a deep admiration within
me during those early years. My ensuing creative practice has been shaped by my
undergraduate studies in Industrial Design and diverse professional experiences. In this time,
I have explored the design process in areas like innovative product development, user-centric
methodologies, and systems thinking. This ability to use scientific advancements to create
new products and services that drive business and economy and at the same time make
people’s lives easier and more comfortable is something that excites and motivates me to
build a long-term career in this field.

I pursued my Bachelor’s degree from India’s premier design school, the National Institute of
Design (NID), where my design thinking and creativity took a decisively humane and people-
oriented direction. During my time at NID, I was introduced to three facets of design: systems
design, service design, and interaction design. The systems approach taught me to look at a
problem area in its entirety before identifying potential interventions, while service design
focused on solving problems through technological interventions. But interaction design
appealed to me the most due to its user-centricity and accessible designs.

In college, I took on multiple design assignments that further helped me identify my design
niche. For my graduation assignment with Grant Thornton, I worked with indigenous bamboo
artisans from Assam to revive endangered Japi crafts and saw firsthand how design had the
unique power to effect social change. For a similar project, by using a participatory design
approach, I designed a mechanical tool that alleviated the physical strain and increased the
productivity of flower vendors engaged in garland weaving activities. I also used behavioral
mapping to understand the challenges faced by pedestrians and drivers, designed a
lightweight, highly visible construction barricade to improve safety for pedestrians during
peak traffic hours.

Beyond these community-based projects, I worked on two tech-intensive projects. In the first,
I analyzed STI management practices and barriers restricting access to services among female
sex workers (FSWs) in Bhopal. Employing snowball sampling techniques to locate their work
zones and, using methods like GIGA mapping user journeys, I developed a Trigger and
Response Model to better interpret the data. The project led to recommendations for


--- Page 18 ---
community-centric support systems such as mobile clinics and awareness programs. In the
second project I created an educational activity kit to help children explore self-identity. By
utilizing user journey mapping, participatory testing, and iterative prototyping, I built a tool
to help children understand and express their feelings, which was later presented and
published at the International Conference on Research into Design (ICoRD’25).


My myriad set of formative learnings has coalesced into my passion for making a career in
human-centered design and user experience research. I have come to appreciate that product
design albeit a creative process, requires conversance with software design tools, user-centric
methodologies, and an allied understanding of socio-economic dynamics and business
management to truly understand the consumer ask. While I have been working on developing
the aforementioned proficiencies, I require advanced training and international exposure to
the field which I hope to gain through the MS Human Centered Design & Engineering at
University of Washington.

3. Describe your background and your academic experience *
Having earned my Bachelor's degree from the leading design institution in India, the National Institute
of Design (NID), my design thinking, creativity, and critical problem-solving have been greatly
influenced by a strong people-oriented perspective.
Throughout my academic journey, I have maintained a consistent scorecard and earned the Highest
Scorer award in my graduating cohort. But while my GPA of 8.6 in my Bachelor's in Industrial Design
provides a glimpse into my academic progress, I believe the essence of design goes beyond
conventional grading metrics and is demonstrated through practical application and impact.
My graduation project with Grant Thornton, where I worked with Assamese indigenous bamboo
artists to revive the endangered Japi crafts, was a turning point in my academic career. Immersion in
their culture helped me to better appreciate community-driven design and its obvious influence. In
another project, I rebuilt construction barricades to improve safety for pedestrians and vehicle
operators. Using behavioral mapping, I found difficulties experienced by rickshaw/two-wheeler
drivers and pedestrians, so I guided the design of a lightweight, highly visible barrier with simple
installation and maintenance.
Beyond these, I have produced an instructional activity kit examining the effect of touch on self-
identity for youngsters and a mechanical tool to increase productivity for garland suppliers, with the
former being chosen for presentation and publication at the International Conference on Research
into Design (ICoRD25). Every one of these encounters has strengthened my ability to tackle sensitive
and challenging topics with a drive to find appropriate solutions.


--- Page 22 ---
From a bird’s-eye perspective, all my projects have reiterated the interconnection of design, utility,
and sustainability. This understanding has been further strengthened through my professional
experiences—at Thinkonomers (HDL), where I learned the value of user feedback; at Pichkaari Design
Studio, where I worked on rebranding and user flow enhancement; at Grant Thornton; and now as a
UX/UI Designer at BRND Studio, where I manage end-to-end design and research for SaaS dashboards
and educational platforms—this knowledge has been further reinforced. These encounters have
informed my design philosophy: designing simple, user-first experiences that carefully combine
human-centered knowledge with logic.
4. Describe how you would use the qualification to address challenges faced by society in your
home country, upholding the values of social justice and environmental stewardship *
Service design has the potential to make services more inclusive, efficient, and sustainable,
transforming their delivery and experience. Growing up in India with large amounts of human capital,
I have often seen that, although there is no shortage of hard work, a lack of organized and simple
mechanisms keeps that effort from having an actual impact. The difficulty is working smart rather than
only harder.
From my experiences, small-scale businesses and the industry of traditional crafts clearly show some
of the most obvious places this disparity exists, which hampers novel initiatives like corporate social
responsibility programs too. Many local businesses and artists have wonderful abilities, but their work
is often overlooked and underappreciated without well-designed systems linking them to the correct
markets. By simplifying supply chains, integrating technology, and guaranteeing these companies can
run sustainably while safeguarding cultural legacies, service design can help close this distance.
Working with artists, I observed that merely altering the positioning and sale of their goods had a
significant impact on their livelihoods.
Beyond this, service design can improve working conditions too. Many developing Indian companies
battle ineffective processes, which cause employee burnout and disengagement. Companies require
answers catered to their unique problems rather than imposing systems and structures fashioned for
international companies. Service design offers a structure to reimagine these systems—balancing
workloads, altering roles, and supporting a more effective, employee- and consumer-centric
approach.
Public services also stand to be very much beneficial. For many user groups, complicated government
processes and inaccessible infrastructures cause everyday hardships, as discovered during multiple
projects. Whether by revamping these systems—digital interventions, process restructuring, or better
information accessibility and strategy development—we may make necessary services more
compassionate and user-friendly.
Equally important is the role that service design plays in environmental sustainability. Many times,
India's rapid economic expansion comes at the cost of environmental well-being. Whether in waste
management, urban planning, or responsible consumption, including sustainable practices in regular
services will help us advance without sacrificing the earth. India has enormous potential; by using
human-centered solutions, we can design systems that empower people, safeguard the environment,
and produce significant, long-lasting change.

3. Describe your background and your academic experience *

artists to revive the endangered Japi crafts, was a turning point in my academic career. Immersion in
their culture helped me to better appreciate community-driven design and its obvious influence. In
another project, I rebuilt construction barricades to improve safety for pedestrians and vehicle
operators. Using behavioral mapping, I found difficulties experienced by rickshaw/two-wheeler
drivers and pedestrians, so I guided the design of a lightweight, highly visible barrier with simple
installation and maintenance.
Beyond these, I have produced an instructional activity kit examining the effect of touch on self-
identity for youngsters and a mechanical tool to increase productivity for garland suppliers, with the
former being chosen for presentation and publication at the International Conference on Research
into Design (ICoRD25). Every one of these encounters has strengthened my ability to tackle sensitive
and challenging topics with a drive to find appropriate solutions.

run sustainably while safeguarding cultural legacies, service design can help close this distance.
Working with artists, I observed that merely altering the positioning and sale of their goods had a

Addressing STI Management Challenges Among
Female Sex Workers in India
Abstract. I have always been passionate about tackling social issues that affect communities often neglected
due to discrimination, stereotypes, and pre-defined societal norms. In one of my research projects, I took a
holistic approach to explore societal systems and focused on the challenges faced by female sex workers
(FSWs) in India. Through this work, I identified a significant gap: the lack of attention to the behaviors and
systems of stakeholders involved in managing sexually transmitted infections (STIs) among FSWs and the
limited awareness of STIs among FSWs themselves. This project aims to address these barriers by employing
service design methodologies to improve access to healthcare facilities and enhance the effectiveness of
STI-related interventions for FSWs.
1. Literature Review
Female sex workers (FSWs) in India encounter a multitude of healthcare access barriers, among
which stigma, legal constraints, and a healthcare infrastructure not aligned with their needs severely
limit their access to much-needed care. The discrimination against sex workers in India is deeply
entrenched. Historically, by 1869, FSWs who tested positive for sexually transmitted infections (STIs)
were imprisoned. As a result, many kept their profession a secret and refrained from getting tested due
to concerns about social rejection and fear of incarceration. In the post-colonial era, the HIV crisis of
the 1980s exposed significant shortcomings in the healthcare system and underscored the critical
importance of STI prevention and public education [1].
Estimates suggest that FSWs in India contribute substantially to HIV transmission, accounting for
71,000 documented cases [2]. While several services are available to support FSWs, organizations
like the Centre for Advanced Research and Development-Targeted Initiative (CARD-TI) have made
strides in raising awareness and offering assistance [3]. However, the reach of such programs remains
limited due to the fear of identity exposure and the persistent discrimination FSWs face.
The World Health Organization’s (WHO) program for STI prevention emphasizes evidence-based
services
characterized
by
high
quality,
optimized
processes
and
partnerships,
data-driven
decision-making, community engagement, and innovation [4]. Unfortunately, the protocols currently
implemented in India fall short of these recommendations, necessitating an urgent reevaluation and
enhancement of existing strategies to align with global best practices.
Socially, FSWs experience acute levels of isolation and limited access to vital support networks [5].
Economically, stigma restricts opportunities, trapping many in cycles of poverty and increasing their
vulnerability to exploitation by clients and law enforcement [6]. Legally, FSWs face harassment and
abuse from authorities with little to no judicial recourse [7]. From a healthcare perspective, fear of
stigma discourages FSWs from seeking medical advice, resulting in untreated STIs and exacerbated
health conditions due to discriminatory practices in healthcare settings [8]. On a personal level,
persistent discrimination erodes their self-worth and mental health, contributing to low self-esteem
and psychological distress [9].
In light of these challenges, this topic warrants urgent attention and action. A project focused on
addressing the healthcare access barriers for FSWs in India can contribute to reducing the stigma they
face, enhancing the effectiveness of public health interventions, and improving the overall quality of
life for this marginalized population.


--- Page 29 ---
2. Proposed Research Methodology
Targeted research methods can be used to engage stakeholders in STI management for FSWs and understand the
barriers in detail. Identifying obstacles as perceived by primary and secondary stakeholders will help collect
tailored data to analyze the layers of systems around FSWs and STIs. According to a 2022 study, there are over
8 lakh identified female sex workers in India [10], though many remain unidentified due to intersectional stigma
related to sex, gender, and patriarchal attitudes. Snowball sampling, which relies on trust-building with an initial
participant, can help reach this hidden population.
Interviews with FSWs can highlight their perceptions of STIs and barriers to healthcare, while focus group
discussions can compare the experiences of NGO-affiliated FSWs with those who are not. Observational studies
at ART centers and ICTCs can provide insights into current treatment protocols, counseling practices, and
challenges faced by STI counselors working with high-risk populations. [11]
Techniques such as fly-on-the-wall observation and immersive activities, effective in past projects with
service-oriented populations, could reveal dynamics in healthcare interactions. This research aims to map the
broader system around FSWs and identify key intervention points to improve their access to medical facilities.
3. Potential Outcomes and Challenges
In a previous project, sex workers mentioned their fear of going to hospitals alone due to the fear of judgment.
With 1,160 "Suraksha Clinics" (STI/RTI clinics) in district-level government healthcare facilities, the NACO
ensures STI services are free and adhere to uniform care standards in family planning and reproductive health
[12]. A service could be developed to address the challenge of disseminating the right messages to the
community through various existing and new channels and to create a companionship model to encourage them
to access these services.
Potential challenges in addressing STIs among female sex workers (FSWs) include their discomfort in sharing
personal details like residence or contact information due to societal stigma and fear of exposure. Leveraging
technology for anonymous consultations could help FSWs seek medical advice discreetly. Collaborations
between NGOs like CARD-TI and healthcare providers could also create trust-based models where NGOs act as
intermediaries, facilitating access to healthcare [11]. The diagnostic process, involving personal interviews about
sexual history and profession, may be distressing for FSWs. Training healthcare providers to handle sensitive
topics empathetically could ease these interactions. Tools like flashcards or visual indicators could enable FSWs
to share personal information more comfortably, fostering trust and improving engagement with healthcare
systems.
In the past, I have worked with communities that are challenging to engage with due to factors such as building
trust, identification of the right stakeholders, and communication barriers. However, for each target group, I
have been motivated to tackle these challenges using unique research methodologies and creating solutions that
benefit the community. With a background in research and design, I believe I can strengthen my existing
knowledge at the postgraduate level, leveraging the knowledge gained to its fullest potential. This will allow me
to take on more complex briefs, fostering personal growth and contributing to societal development through
design challenges.


--- Page 30 ---

Project Proposal:
ABSTRACT
I have always been passionate about tackling social issues that affect communities often neglected
due to discrimination, stereotypes, and pre-defined societal norms. In one of my research projects, I
took a holistic approach to explore societal systems and focused on the challenges faced by female
sex workers (FSWs) in India. Through this work, I identified a significant gap: the lack of attention to
the behaviors and systems of stakeholders involved in managing sexually transmitted infections
(STIs) among FSWs and the limited awareness of STIs among FSWs themselves. This project aims
to address these barriers by employing service design methodologies to improve access to healthcare
facilities and enhance the effectiveness of STI-related interventions for FSWs.
RATIONALE

among which stigma, legal constraints, and a healthcare infrastructure not aligned with their
needs severely limit their access to much-needed care. The discrimination against sex
